1347 : Mal 5.45 b|Mal 5.45b: asumpaṅ cintamani arja (a gem or a flower?). It is used to denote a partic. part of man's interior (also cintyamaṇi, cittamaṇi or nala cintamaṇi, something like ``heart-jewel''), a central point in the samādhi. So it occurs in the names of various kinds of samādhi:  cintāmaṇi

2533 : Mal 16.13 |Mal 16.13: keraṅan taṅ stri luṅâlabuh paruṅ lyan akĕnḍat anâjar-ajara. In ModJ. ṅĕṇḍat is used for all sorts of suicide -- hanging, drowning or jumping over cliffs -- but for hanging in particular there exists the term ṅĕṇḍat tali. The examples above, however, show that akĕṇḍat is distinct from both alabuh er and alabuh paruṅ. The ModJ. meaning of ``to break off'' appears to be absent.  kĕṇḍat*
